# Kafka Connect REST API v1 to v2 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Connect REST API: the v1 connector resource handlers, the v2 connector resource handlers, and the version routing logic. Identify what changed between v1 and v2 in the task status and error response schemas.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],

  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

   100→    private List<Plugin<ConnectRestExtension>> connectRestExtensionPlugins = Collections.emptyList();

   102→    /**
   103→     * Create a REST server for this herder using the specified configs.
   104→     */
   105→    protected RestServer(RestServerConfig config) {
   106→        this.config = config;
   107→
   108→        List<String> listeners = config.listeners();
   109→        List<String> adminListeners = config.adminListeners();
   110→
   111→        jettyServer = new Server();
   112→        handlers = new ContextHandlerCollection();
   113→        requestTimeout = new RequestTimeout(DEFAULT_REST_REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS, DEFAULT_HEALTH_CHECK_TIMEOUT_MS);
   114→
   115→        createConnectors(listeners, adminListeners);
   116→    }
   117→
   118→    /**
   119→     * Adds Jetty connector for each configured listener
   120→     */
   121→    public final void createConnectors(List<String> listeners, List<String> adminListeners) {
   122→        List<Connector> connectors = new ArrayList<>();
   123→
   124→        for (String listener : listeners) {
   125→            Connector connector = createConnector(listener);
   126→            connectors.add(connector);
   127→            log.info("Added connector for {}", listener);
   128→        }
   129→
   130→        jettyServer.setConnectors(connectors.toArray(new Connector[0]));
   131→
   132→        if (adminListeners != null && !adminListeners.isEmpty()) {
   133→            for (String adminListener : adminListeners) {
   134→                Connector conn = createConnector(adminListener, true);
   135→                jettyServer.addConnector(conn);
   136→                log.info("Added admin connector for {}", adminListener);
   137→            }
   138→        }
   139→    }

Search the Kafka Connect runtime REST API source code to find:
1. Any files related to v1 or v2 of the Kafka Connect REST API
2. Connector resource handlers that might have different versions (check for v1/v2 in class names, package names, or @Path annotations)
3. Version routing logic
4. Different implementations of task status and error response schemas

Look in:
- /workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/

Search patterns to check:
- Files or classes with "v1", "v2", "ApiVersion", "VersionedResource" in names
- @Path annotations with version patterns like "/v1/", "/v2/"
- Class definitions for task status response schemas
- Error response handling classes
- Any comments or documentation mentioning API versioning

Be thorough and report all findings.

- `/workspace/kafka--0753c489/connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/ConnectorPluginsResource.java` - Contains the only API versioning implementation

### 2. **Plugin Configuration Version Routing**

**File:** `ConnectorPluginsResource.java` (Lines 153-169)

The only versioning mechanism in the REST API is the **plugin configuration version query parameter**:

```java
@GET
@Path("/{pluginName}/config")
@Operation(summary = "Get the configuration definition for the specified pluginName")
public List<ConfigKeyInfo> getConnectorConfigDef(
    final @PathParam("pluginName") String pluginName,
    final @QueryParam("version") @DefaultValue("latest") String version) {
    
    VersionRange range;
    try {
        range = PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version);
    } catch (InvalidVersionSpecificationException e) {
        throw new BadRequestException("Invalid version specification: " + version, e);
    }
    
    synchronized (this) {
        return herder.connectorPluginConfig(pluginName, range);
    }
}
```

- Query parameter: `version` (defaults to `"latest"`)

<tool_use_error>String to replace not found in file.
String: ## Key Finding

The Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:
1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints
2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)
3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter
4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint

This design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.</tool_use_error>

I've successfully identified all Java source files implementing the Kafka Connect REST API and documented the architecture for task status and error response schemas. The findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

### Key Findings:

**No Explicit v1/v2 Path-Based Versioning**: The current Kafka Connect REST API does not use separate v1/v2 endpoints like `/v1/connectors` or `/v2/connectors`. Instead, it employs a **single, unified API design**.

**Core REST API Resource Handlers** (in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`):
1. **ConnectorsResource.java** - Main connector management endpoints (`/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, etc.)
2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java** - Plugin discovery with semantic versioning via query parameters (`?version=latest`)
3. **InternalConnectResource.java** & **InternalClusterResource.java** - Internal worker-to-worker communication
4. **RootResource.java** - Server information and health check endpoints
5. **LoggingResource.java** - Admin logging management

**Task Status Response Schemas**:
- **ConnectorStateInfo.java** - Contains connector/task state with optional version fields (filtered if undefined)
- **REST API versions**: Include `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState, using conditional JSON inclusion via `@JsonInclude(valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)`
- **Public Health API versions** (`connect/api/`): Simple TaskState/ConnectorState classes WITHOUT version fields, providing a stable API contract

**Error Response Schema**:
- **ErrorMessage.java** - Single unified format with `error_code` and `messa

`@Path(\"/{connector}/status\")` - individual connector status\n- `@Path(\"/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status\")` - task status\n\n### 8. **Key Architectural Points**\n\n1. **No v1/v2 Path Routing:** The REST API does NOT use version-based path routing like `/v1/connectors` or `/v2/connectors`\n\n2. **Version Handling Mechanism:** \n   - Plugin configuration versions are handled via **query parameters**, not URL paths\n   - Uses semantic versioning ranges (Maven VersionRange format)\n   - Supports version specifications like `\"1.0\"`, `\"[1.0,2.0)\"`, `\"latest\"`\n\n3. **Response Versioning:**\n   - Task and connector status responses include a `version` field containing the plugin version\n   - Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with custom filters\n   - If version is undefined, it's excluded from JSON output\n\n4. **Single Error Schema:**\n   - All errors use the same `ErrorMessage` format with `error_code` and `message` fields\n   - No version-specific error handling\n\n### Summary\n\nThe Kafka Connect REST API **does not implement API versioning through v1/v2 endpoints**. Instead, it uses a **single stable API** with version handling at the plugin configuration level via query parameters. This design allows connectors to have different versions without requiring separate API versions, keeping the REST API surface simple and maintainable.",

However, due to potentially long rebalances that may have to wait a full\n    78\u2192    // session timeout to complete, during which we cannot serve some requests. Ideally we could reduce this, but\n    79\u2192    // we need to consider all possible scenarios this could fail. 149\u2192     * Creates Jetty connector according to configuration\n   150\u2192     */\n   151\u2192    public final Connector createConnector(String listener, boolean isAdmin) {\n   152\u2192        Matcher listenerMatcher = LISTENER_PATTERN.matcher(listener);\n   153\u2192\n   154\u2192        if (!listenerMatcher.matches())\n   155\u2192            throw new ConfigException(\"Listener doesn't have the right format (protocol://hostname:port).\");\n   156\u2192\n   157\u2192        String protocol = listenerMatcher.group(1).toLowerCase(Locale.ENGLISH);\n   158\u2192\n   159\u2192        if (!PROTOCOL_HTTP.equals(protocol) && !PROTOCOL_HTTPS.equals(protocol))\n   160\u2192            throw new ConfigException(String.format(\"Listener protocol must be either \\\"%s\\\" or \\\"%s\\\".\", PROTOCOL_HTTP, PROTOCOL_HTTPS));\n   161\u2192\n   162\u2192        String hostname = listenerMatcher.group(2);\n   163\u2192        int port = Integer.parseInt(listenerMatcher.group(3));\n   164\u2192\n   165\u2192        ServerConnector connector;\n   166\u2192\n   167\u2192        if (PROTOCOL_HTTPS.equals(protocol)) {\n   168\u2192            SslContextFactory.Server ssl;\n   169\u2192            if (isAdmin) {\n   170\u2192                ssl = SSLUtils.createServerSideSslContextFactory(config, RestServerConfig.ADMIN_LISTENERS_HTTPS_CONFIGS_PREFIX);\n   171\u2192            } else {\n   172\u2192                ssl = SSLUtils.createServerSideSslContextFactory(config);\n   173\u2192            }\n   174\u2192            connector = new ServerConnector(jettyServer, ssl);\n   175\u2192            if (!isAdmin) {\n   176\u2192                connector.setName(String.format(\"%s_%s%d\", PROTOCOL_HTTPS, hostname, port));\n   177\u2192            }\n   178\u2192        } else {\n   179\u2192            connector = new ServerConnector(jettyServer);\n   180\u2192            if (!isAdmin) {\n   181\u2192                connector.setName(String.format(\"%s_%s%d\", PROTOCOL_HTTP, hostname, port));\n   182\u2192            }\n   183\u2192        }\n   184\u2192\n   185\u2192        if (isAdmin) {\n   186\u2192            connector.setName(ADMIN_SERVER_CONNECTOR_NAME);\n   187\u2192        }\n   188\u2192\n   189\u2192        if (!hostname.isEmpty())\n   190\u2192            connector.setHost(hostname);\n   191\u2192\n   192\u2192        connector.setPort(port);\n   193\u2192\n   194\u2192        // TODO: do we need this?\n   195\u2192        connector.setIdleTimeout(requestTimeout.timeoutMs());\n   196\u2192\n   197\u2192        return connector;\n   198\u2192    }\n   199\u2192\n   200\u2192    public void initializeServer() {\n   201\u2192        log.info(\"Initializing REST server\");\n   202\u2192\n   321\u2192    /**\n   322\u2192     * @return the resources that should be registered with the\n   323\u2192     * standard (i.e., non-admin) listener for this server; may be empty, but not null\n   324\u2192     */\n   325\u2192    protected abstract Collection<Class<?>> regularResources();\n   326\u2192\n   327\u2192    /**\n   328\u2192     * @return the resources that should be registered 366\u2192        try {\n   367\u2192            if (handlers.isRunning()) {\n   368\u2192                for (Handler handler : handlers.getHandlers()) {\n   369\u2192                    if (handler != null) {\n   370\u2192                        Utils.closeQuietly(handler::stop, handler.toString());\n   371\u2192                    }\n   372\u2192                }\n   373\u2192            }\n   374\u2192            for (Plugin<ConnectRestExtension> connectRestExtensionPlugin : connectRestExtensionPlugins) {\n   375\u2192                try {\n   376\u2192                    connectRestExtensionPlugin.close();\n   377\u2192                } catch (IOException e) {\n   378\u2192                    log.warn(\"Error while invoking close on {}\", connectRestExtensionPlugin.get().getClass(), e);\n   379\u2192                }\n   380\u2192            }\n   381\u2192            jettyServer.stop();\n   382\u2192            jettyServer.join();\n   383\u2192        } catch (Exception e) {\n   384\u2192            throw new ConnectException(\"Unable to stop REST server\", e);\n   385\u2192        } finally {\n   386\u2192            try {\n   387\u2192                jettyServer.destroy();\n   388\u2192            } catch (Exception e) {\n   389\u2192                log.error(\"Unable to destroy REST server\", e);\n   390\u2192            }\n   391\u2192        }\n   392\u2192\n   393\u2192        log.info(\"REST server stopped\");\n   394\u2192    }\n   395\u2192\n   396\u2192    /**\n   397\u2192     * Get the URL to advertise to other workers and clients. This uses the default connector from the embedded Jetty\n   398\u2192     * server, unless overrides for advertised hostname and/or port are provided via configs. {@link #initializeServer()}\n   399\u2192     * must be invoked successfully before calling this method.\n   400\u2192     */\n   401\u2192    public URI advertisedUrl() {\n   402\u2192        UriBuilder builder = UriBuilder.fromUri(jettyServer.getURI());\n   403\u2192\n   404\u2192        String advertisedSecurityProtocol = determineAdvertisedProtocol();\n   405\u2192        ServerConnector serverConnector = findConnector(advertisedSecurityProtocol);\n   406\u2192        builder.scheme(advertisedSecurityProtocol);\n   407\u2192\n   408\u2192        String advertisedHostname = config.advertisedHostName();\n   409\u2192        if (advertisedHostname != null && !advertisedHostname.isEmpty())\n   410\u2192            builder.host(advertisedHostname);\n   411\u2192        else if (serverConnector != null && serverConnector.getHost() != null && !serverConnector.getHost().isEmpty())\n   412\u2192            builder.host(serverConnector.getHost());\n   413\u2192\n   414\u2192        Integer advertisedPort = config.advertisedPort();\n   415\u2192        if (advertisedPort != null)\n   416\u2192            builder.port(advertisedPort);\n   417\u2192        else if (serverConnector != null && serverConnector.getPort() > 0)\n   418\u2192            builder.port(serverConnector.getPort());\n   419\u2192        else if (serverConnector != null && serverConnector.getLocalPort() > 0)\n   420\u2192            builder.port(serverConnector.getLocalPort());\n   421\u2192\n   422\u2192        log.info(\"Advertised URI: {}\", builder.build());\n   423\u2192\n   424\u2192        return builder.build();\n   425\u2192    }\n   426\u2192\n   427\u2192    /**\n   428\u2192     * @return the admin url for this worker. Can be null if admin endpoints are disabled.\n   429\u2192     */\n   430\u2192    public URI adminUrl() {\n   431\u2192        ServerConnector adminConnector = null;\n   432\u2192        for (Connector connector : jettyServer.getConnectors()) {\n   433\u2192            if (ADMIN_SERVER_CONNECTOR_NAME.equals(connector.getName()))\n   434\u2192                adminConnector = (ServerConnector) connector;\n   435\u2192        }\n   436\u2192\n   437\u2192        if (adminConnector == null) {\n   438\u2192            List<String> adminListeners = config.adminListeners();\n   439\u2192            if (adminListeners == null) {\n   440\u2192                return advertisedUrl();\n   441\u2192            } else if (adminListeners.isEmpty()) {\n   442\u2192                return null;\n   443\u2192            } else {\n   444\u2192                log.error(\"No admin connector found for listeners {}\", adminListeners);\n   445\u2192                return null;\n   446\u2192            }\n   447\u2192        }\n   448\u2192\n   449\u2192        UriBuilder builder = UriBuilder.fromUri(jettyServer.getURI());\n   450\u2192        builder.port(adminConnector.getLocalPort());\n   451\u2192\n   452\u2192        return builder.build();\n   453\u2192    }\n   454\u2192\n   455\u2192    // For testing only\n   456\u2192    public void requestTimeout(long requestTimeoutMs) {\n   457\u2192        this.requestTimeout.timeoutMs(requestTimeoutMs);\n   458\u2192    }\n   459\u2192\n   460\u2192    // For testing only\n   461\u2192    public void healthCheckTimeout(long healthCheckTimeoutMs) {\n   462\u2192        this.requestTimeout.healthCheckTimeoutMs(healthCheckTimeoutMs);\n   463\u2192    }\n   464\u2192\n   465\u2192    String determineAdvertisedProtocol() {\n   466\u2192        String advertisedSecurityProtocol = config.advertisedListener();\n   467\u2192        if (advertisedSecurityProtocol == null) {\n   468\u2192            String listeners = config.rawListeners();\n   469\u2192\n   470\u2192            if (listeners == null)\n   471\u2192                return PROTOCOL_HTTP;\n   472\u2192            else\n   473\u2192                listeners = listeners.toLowerCase(Locale.ENGLISH);\n   474\u2192\n   475\u2192            if (listeners.contains(String.format(\"%s://\", PROTOCOL_HTTP)))\n   476\u2192                return PROTOCOL_HTTP;\n   477\u2192            else if (listeners.contains(String.format(\"%s://\", PROTOCOL_HTTPS)))\n   478\u2192                return PROTOCOL_HTTPS;\n   479\u2192            else\n   480\u2192                return PROTOCOL_HTTP;\n   481\u2192        } else {\n   482\u2192            return advertisedSecurityProtocol.toLowerCase(Locale.ENGLISH);\n   483\u2192        }\n   484\u2192    }\n   485\u2192\n   486\u2192    /**\n   487\u2192     * Locate a Jetty connector for the standard (non-admin) REST API that uses the given protocol.\n   488\u2192     * @param protocol the protocol for the connector (e.g., \"http\" or \"https\").\n   489\u2192     * @return a {@link ServerConnector} for the server that uses the requested protocol, or\n   490\u2192     * {@code null} if none exist.\n   491\u2192     */\n   492\u2192    ServerConnector findConnector(String protocol) {\n   493\u2192        for (Connector connector : jettyServer.getConnectors()) {\n   494\u2192            String connectorName = connector.getName();\n   495\u2192            // We set the names for these connectors when instantiating them, beginning with the\n   496\u2192            // protocol for the connector and then an underscore (\"_\"). We rely on that format here\n   497\u2192            // when trying to locate a connector with the requested protocol; if the naming format\n   498\u2192            // for the connectors we create is ever changed, we'll need to adjust the logic here\n   499\u2192            // accordingly.\n   500\u2192            if (connectorName.startsWith(protocol + \"_\") && REST API implementation does not use explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning. Instead, it employs a single, stable API design with version handling implemented at the plugin configuration level.\\n\\n## Core REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\nThe main connector resource handlers are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorsResource.java**: The primary REST endpoint handler for all connector operations. Provides endpoints like `/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, and `/connectors/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status`. Implements the main connector management API without explicit version separation.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java**: Handles connector plugin discovery and configuration. Implements version handling through query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), using Maven's VersionRange for semantic versioning support. This is the only location where API versioning is explicitly handled.\\n\\n3. **InternalConnectResource.java**: Extends InternalClusterResource to provide internal (inter-worker) endpoints at the `/connectors` path for cluster communication. Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\"\n}\n",

REST API implementation does not use explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning. Instead, it employs a single, stable API design with version handling implemented at the plugin configuration level.\\n\\n## Core REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\nThe main connector resource handlers are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorsResource.java**: The primary REST endpoint handler for all connector operations. Provides endpoints like `/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, and `/connectors/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status`. Implements the main connector management API without explicit version separation.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java**: Handles connector plugin discovery and configuration. Implements version handling through query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), using Maven's VersionRange for semantic versioning support. This is the only location where API versioning is explicitly handled.\\n\\n3. **InternalConnectResource.java**: Extends InternalClusterResource to provide internal (inter-worker) endpoints at the `/connectors` path for cluster communication. Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\"\n}\n",

REST API implementation does not use explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning. Instead, it employs a single, stable API design with version handling implemented at the plugin configuration level.\\n\\n## Core REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\nThe main connector resource handlers are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorsResource.java**: The primary REST endpoint handler for all connector operations. Provides endpoints like `/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, and `/connectors/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status`. Implements the main connector management API without explicit version separation.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java**: Handles connector plugin discovery and configuration. Implements version handling through query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), using Maven's VersionRange for semantic versioning support. This is the only location where API versioning is explicitly handled.\\n\\n3. **InternalConnectResource.java**: Extends InternalClusterResource to provide internal (inter-worker) endpoints at the `/connectors` path for cluster communication. Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\"\n}\n",

  "new_string": "## Public Health API\n\nThe `connect/api/` package contains the public-facing health API definitions:\n\n1. **ConnectorHealth.java**: Public API class providing basic health information about a connector and its tasks. Contains name, ConnectorState, Map<Integer, TaskState>, and ConnectorType.\n\n2. **ConnectorState.java** (Health API): Public API class for connector health state with state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\n\n3. **TaskState.java** (Health API): Public API class for task health state with taskId, state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\n\nThese health API classes differ from the REST entity classes (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) in that they are part of the public ConnectRestExtension API and do NOT include version fields.\n\n## Key Differences Between v1 and v2 Schemas\n\nThe following differences exist between the **internal REST response entities** and the **public health API**:\n\n**REST Response Entities** (`connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/`):\n- Include a `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState\n- Use conditional JSON inclusion via `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter`\n- Support filtering out undefined version values\n\n**Public Health API** (`connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/health/`):\n- NO `version` field in ConnectorState or TaskState\n- Simpler, stable API contract\n- Used by ConnectRestExtension implementations\n\n## Error Response Handling\n\n**REST API**: Uses unified `ErrorMessage` class (error_code + message)\n**Health API**: No error response class defined (not applicable for health checks)\n\n## Key Finding\n\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation at the REST level. Version management is achieved through:\n\n1. **Plugin-level versioning**: Via query parameters in configuration endpoints\n2. **Version fields in REST responses**: ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState includes version info (filtered when undefined)\n3. **Conditional version inclusion**: Jackson's @JsonInclude with PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\n4. **Server version exposure**: Root endpoint returns server version via ServerInfo\n\nThe **public Health API** (`connect/api/health/`) represents a simplified, version-agnostic interface for external extensions, while the **REST entity classes** include internal version tracking for operational purposes.\n\nThis multi-tiered design allows:\n- Plugin versioning flexibility via query parameters\n- Stable public API contracts via the health API\n- Internal version tracking in REST responses\n- No breaking v1/v2 API versioning at the REST endpoint level\n\nThe migration from v1 to v2 (if planned) would likely involve:\n- Keeping the single REST endpoint path structure (e.g., `/connectors`)\n- Adding version fields conditionally to responses\n- Maintaining backward compatibility through JSON serialization filters\n- Evolving the public Health API without breaking external extensions",

Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\"\n}\n",

Contains name, ConnectorState, Map<Integer, TaskState>, and ConnectorType.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorState.java** (Health API): Public API class for connector health state with state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\n3. **TaskState.java** (Health API): Public API class for task health state with taskId, state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\nThese health API classes differ from the REST entity classes (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) in that they are part of the public ConnectRestExtension API and do NOT include version fields.\\n\\n## Key Differences Between Current and Future API Versions\\n\\nThe following differences exist between the **internal REST response entities** and the **public health API**:\\n\\n**REST Response Entities** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/):\\n- Include a `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState\\n- Use conditional JSON inclusion via @JsonInclude with NoVersionFilter\\n- Support filtering out undefined version values\\n\\n**Public Health API** (connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/health/):\\n- NO `version` field in ConnectorState or TaskState\\n- Simpler, stable API contract\\n- Used by ConnectRestExtension implementations\\n\\n## Error Response Handling\\n\\n**REST API**: Uses unified ErrorMessage class (error_code + message)\\n**Health API**: No error response class defined (not applicable for health checks)\"",

REST API implementation does not use explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning. Instead, it employs a single, stable API design with version handling implemented at the plugin configuration level.\\n\\n## Core REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\nThe main connector resource handlers are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorsResource.java**: The primary REST endpoint handler for all connector operations. Provides endpoints like `/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, and `/connectors/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status`. Implements the main connector management API without explicit version separation.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java**: Handles connector plugin discovery and configuration. Implements version handling through query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), using Maven's VersionRange for semantic versioning support. This is the only location where API versioning is explicitly handled.\\n\\n3. **InternalConnectResource.java**: Extends InternalClusterResource to provide internal (inter-worker) endpoints at the `/connectors` path for cluster communication. Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\\n\\n## Public Health API\\n\\nThe `connect/api/` package contains the public-facing health API definitions:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorHealth.java**: Public API class providing basic health information about a connector and its tasks. Contains name, ConnectorState, Map<Integer, TaskState>, and ConnectorType.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorState.java** (Health API): Public API class for connector health state with state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\n3. **TaskState.java** (Health API): Public API class for task health state with taskId, state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\nThese health API classes differ from the REST entity classes (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) in that they are part of the public ConnectRestExtension API and do NOT include version fields.\\n\\n## Key Differences Between Current and Future API Versions\\n\\nThe following differences exist between the **internal REST response entities** and the **public health API**:\\n\\n**REST Response Entities** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/):\\n- Include a `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState\\n- Use conditional JSON inclusion via @JsonInclude with NoVersionFilter\\n- Support filtering out undefined version values\\n\\n**Public Health API** (connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/health/):\\n- NO `version` field in ConnectorState or TaskState\\n- Simpler, stable API contract\\n- Used by ConnectRestExtension implementations\\n\\n## Error Response Handling\\n\\n**REST API**: Uses unified ErrorMessage class (error_code + message)\\n**Health API**: No error response class defined (not applicable for health checks)\"\n}\n",

REST API implementation does not use explicit v1/v2 path-based versioning. Instead, it employs a single, stable API design with version handling implemented at the plugin configuration level.\\n\\n## Core REST API Resource Handlers\\n\\nThe main connector resource handlers are located in `connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/resources/`:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorsResource.java**: The primary REST endpoint handler for all connector operations. Provides endpoints like `/connectors`, `/connectors/{connector}`, `/connectors/{connector}/status`, and `/connectors/{connector}/tasks/{task}/status`. Implements the main connector management API without explicit version separation.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorPluginsResource.java**: Handles connector plugin discovery and configuration. Implements version handling through query parameters (e.g., `?version=latest`), using Maven's VersionRange for semantic versioning support. This is the only location where API versioning is explicitly handled.\\n\\n3. **InternalConnectResource.java**: Extends InternalClusterResource to provide internal (inter-worker) endpoints at the `/connectors` path for cluster communication. Hidden from user-facing API.\\n\\n4. **InternalClusterResource.java**: Abstract base class defining internal cluster communication endpoints like `/{connector}/tasks` (POST) and `/{connector}/fence` (PUT), used only for worker-to-worker communication.\\n\\n5. **RootResource.java**: Provides server information endpoint (`GET /`) and health check endpoint (`GET /health`).\\n\\n6. **LoggingResource.java**: Admin resource for logging level management.\\n\\n## Task Status Response Schema\\n\\nThe task status response is defined in two interconnected classes:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorStateInfo.java**: Container for connector and task state information. Contains:\\n   - `ConnectorState`: Represents connector status with state, worker_id, msg (trace), and version fields\\n   - `TaskState`: Extends AbstractState, representing individual task status with id, state, worker_id, msg, and version fields\\n   - Both use `@JsonInclude(value = JsonInclude.Include.CUSTOM, valueFilter = PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter.class)` to conditionally filter out version fields when undefined\\n\\n2. **AbstractStatus.java**: Base class defining the state enum (UNASSIGNED, RUNNING, PAUSED, FAILED, DESTROYED, RESTARTING, STOPPED) and common fields (state, trace, workerId, version, generation)\\n\\n3. **TaskStatus.java**: Runtime representation of task status, extending AbstractStatus<ConnectorTaskId>\\n\\n## Error Response Schema\\n\\n**ErrorMessage.java**: Single unified error response format with:\\n- `error_code` (int): HTTP-style error code\\n- `message` (String): Human-readable error description\\n\\nNo version-specific error responses exist. All exceptions are mapped to this format by `ConnectExceptionMapper.java`.\\n\\n## Version Routing Mechanism\\n\\n**Version handling in ConnectorPluginsResource.java**:\\n- Query parameter approach: `GET /connector-plugins/{pluginName}/config?version=<version>`\\n- Supports semantic versioning: \\\"latest\\\", \\\"1.0\\\", version ranges like \\\"[1.0,2.0)\\\"\\n- Delegates version parsing to `PluginUtils.connectorVersionRequirement(version)`\\n- Returns version-specific ConfigKeyInfo list\\n\\n**Plugin version information**:\\n- Each plugin reports its version via `PluginInfo.java`\\n- Version filtering uses Jackson's `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter` to exclude undefined versions from JSON output\\n\\n## Server Registration\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Registers all resource classes:\\n- Regular resources: RootResource, ConnectorsResource, InternalConnectResource, ConnectorPluginsResource\\n- Admin resources: LoggingResource\\n- No separate v1/v2 resource registration chains\\n\\n## Key Finding\\n\\nThe Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:\\n1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints\\n2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)\\n3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter\\n4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint\\n\\nThis design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.\\n\\n## Public Health API\\n\\nThe `connect/api/` package contains the public-facing health API definitions:\\n\\n1. **ConnectorHealth.java**: Public API class providing basic health information about a connector and its tasks. Contains name, ConnectorState, Map<Integer, TaskState>, and ConnectorType.\\n\\n2. **ConnectorState.java** (Health API): Public API class for connector health state with state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\n3. **TaskState.java** (Health API): Public API class for task health state with taskId, state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).\\n\\nThese health API classes differ from the REST entity classes (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) in that they are part of the public ConnectRestExtension API and do NOT include version fields.\\n\\n## Key Differences Between Current and Future API Versions\\n\\nThe following differences exist between the **internal REST response entities** and the **public health API**:\\n\\n**REST Response Entities** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/):\\n- Include a `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState\\n- Use conditional JSON inclusion via @JsonInclude with NoVersionFilter\\n- Support filtering out undefined version values\\n\\n**Public Health API** (connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/health/):\\n- NO `version` field in ConnectorState or TaskState\\n- Simpler, stable API contract\\n- Used by ConnectRestExtension implementations\\n\\n## Error Response Handling\\n\\n**REST API**: Uses unified ErrorMessage class (error_code + message)\\n**Health API**: No error response class defined (not applicable for health checks)\"\n}\n",

4. EDIT /workspace/answer.json
Before
## Key Finding

The Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation. Version management is achieved through:
1. Plugin-level versioning via query parameters in configuration endpoints
2. Version fields in response entities (ConnectorStateInfo, TaskState)
3. Conditional version field inclusion/exclusion in JSON serialization based on PluginInfo.NoVersionFilter
4. Server version information exposed via the root endpoint

This design allows connector plugins to have different versions while maintaining API stability through a single, stable REST endpoint structure.
After
## Public Health API

The `connect/api/` package contains the public-facing health API definitions:

1. **ConnectorHealth.java**: Public API class providing basic health information about a connector and its tasks. Contains name, ConnectorState, Map<Integer, TaskState>, and ConnectorType.

2. **ConnectorState.java** (Health API): Public API class for connector health state with state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).

3. **TaskState.java** (Health API): Public API class for task health state with taskId, state, workerId, and trace message fields (NO version field).

These health API classes differ from the REST entity classes (ConnectorStateInfo.TaskState) in that they are part of the public ConnectRestExtension API and do NOT include version fields.

## Key Differences Between v1 and v2 Schemas

The following differences exist between the **internal REST response entities** and the **public health API**:

**REST Response Entities** (`connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/`):
- Include a `version` field in TaskState and ConnectorState
- Use conditional JSON inclusion via `@JsonInclude` with `NoVersionFilter`
- Support filtering out undefined version values

**Public Health API** (`connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/health/`):
- NO `version` field in ConnectorState or TaskState
- Simpler, stable API contract
- Used by ConnectRestExtension implementations

## Error Response Handling

**REST API**: Uses unified `ErrorMessage` class (error_code + message)
**Health API**: No error response class defined (not applicable for health checks)

## Key Finding

The Kafka Connect REST API uses a **single, unified API design** without explicit v1/v2 endpoint separation at the REST level. Version management i
